   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Dental and alveolar flaps
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Alveolar_flap&amp;redirect=no" title="Alveolar flap">
       Alveolar flap
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        alveolar tap
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        flap
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound, used in some spoken
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
        alveolar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
        flaps
       </a>
       is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɾ]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The terms
       <i>
        tap
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        flap
       </i>
       may be used interchangeably.
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ladefoged" title="Peter Ladefoged">
        Peter Ladefoged
       </a>
       proposed for a while that it may be useful to distinguish between them; however, his usage has been inconsistent and contradicted itself even between different editions of the same text.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The last proposed distinction was that a tap strikes its point of contact directly, as a very brief stop, and a flap strikes the point of contact tangentially: "Flaps are most typically made by retracting the tongue tip behind the alveolar ridge and moving it forward so that it strikes the ridge in passing."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, he later no longer felt that it was a useful distinction to make and preferred to use the word
       <i>
        flap
       </i>
       in all cases.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       For linguists who make the distinction, the coronal tap is transcribed as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɾ]
       </span>
       , and the flap is transcribed as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ᴅ]
       </span>
       , which is not recognized by the IPA. Otherwise, alveolars and dentals are typically called
       <i>
        taps
       </i>
       and other articulations
       <i>
        flaps
       </i>
       . No language contrasts a tap and a flap at the same place of articulation.
      </p>
      <p>
       This sound is often analyzed and thus interpreted by native English-speakers as an
       <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">
        'R-sound'
       </a>
       in many foreign languages. In languages for which the segment is present but not phonemic, it is often an allophone of either an alveolar stop (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiceless dental and alveolar stops">
         t
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Alveolar" title="Voiced dental and alveolar stops">
         d
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , or both) or a
       <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">
        rhotic consonant
       </a>
       (like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
        alveolar trill
       </a>
       or the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_approximant" title="Alveolar approximant">
        alveolar approximant
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       When the alveolar tap is the only rhotic consonant in the language, it may be transcribed
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /r/
       </span>
       although that symbol technically represents the trill.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the alveolar tap:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
         flap
        </a>
        , which means it is produced with a single contraction of the muscles so that the tongue makes very brief contact.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
         dental
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
         alveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated behind upper front teeth or at the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        . It is most often
        <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
         apical
        </a>
        , which means that it is pronounced with the tip of the tongue.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>

         </span>

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /d/
         </span>
         among few Australians. Used more often in Australia than in New Zealand. See
         <a href="/wiki/Australian_English_phonology" title="Australian English phonology">
          Australian English phonology
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Flapping" title="Flapping">
          Flapping
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="tl">
           <a href="/wiki/Filipino_orthography" title="Filipino orthography">
            ba
            <b>
             r
            </b>
            ya
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative">
        <span id="Fricative">
        </span>
        Voiced alveolar tapped fricative
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Voiced alveolar tapped fricative">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Voiced alveolar tapped fricative
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ɾ̞
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA_number" title="IPA number">
          IPA number
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         124 430
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         Listen
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="center">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <div class="mediaContainer" style="width:150px">
            <audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="3.3465759637188" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_1" preload="none" style="width:150px">
             <source data-bandwidth="140629" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (141 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/83/Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/>
             <source data-bandwidth="190968" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/83/Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative.ogg/Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/>
            </audio>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div style="text-align:center">
          <small>
           <a href="/wiki/File:Voiced_alveolar_tapped_fricative.ogg" title="File:Voiced alveolar tapped fricative.ogg">
            source
           </a>
           <span style="font-weight:bold;">
            ·
           </span>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
            help
           </a>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       A tapped fricative is in effect a very brief fricative, with the tongue making the gesture for a tapped stop but not making full contact. This can be indicated in the IPA with the lowering diacritic to show full occlusion did not occur. Flapped fricatives are theoretically possible but are not attested.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_2">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced alveolar tapped fricative:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is tapped fricative, which means the tongue makes a brief obstruction sufficient to create frication.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
         apical
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
         alveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the tip of the tongue at the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_2">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Occurrence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Reported from Turkish in a single source.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YavuzBalcı_26-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-YavuzBalcı-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Tacana_language" title="Tacana language">
        Tacana
       </a>
       per UPSID.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alveolar_nasal_flap">
        Alveolar nasal flap
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Alveolar nasal flap">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Alveolar nasal flap
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ɾ̃
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           n̆
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA_number" title="IPA number">

         </a>

        </td>
       </tr>

        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         Encoding
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
          X-SAMPA
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <code>
          4~
         </code>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_3">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental_and_alveolar_flaps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the alveolar nasal flap:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
         flap
        </a>
        , which means it is produced with a single contraction of the muscles so that the tongue makes very brief contact.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
         alveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        , termed respectively
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
          apical
         </a>
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
          laminal
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a nasal consonant, which means air is allowed to escape through the nose, either exclusively (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
         nasal stops
        </a>
        ) or in addition to through the mouth.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_3">
        Occurrence
       </span>

        <td rowspan="2">
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">
           <span class="fn">
            <span style="white-space:nowrap">
             <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-twenty.ogg" title="About this sound">
              <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c9/En-us-twenty.ogg" title="En-us-twenty.ogg">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [ˈtw̥ɛ̃ɾ̃i]
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
           <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
            (
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              help
             </span>

            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-twenty.ogg" title="File:En-us-twenty.ogg">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              info
             </span>
            </a>
            )
           </small>
          </span>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         'twenty'
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         Allophone of unstressed intervocalic
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /nt/
         </span>
         for some speakers. See
         <a href="/wiki/English_phonology" title="English phonology">
          English phonology
         </a>
         ,
         <br/>
         <a href="/wiki/North_American_English_regional_phonology" title="North American English regional phonology">
          North American English regional phonology
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Flapping" title="Flapping">
          Flapping
         </a>
        </td>

                    Kiel convention (1989)

                </div>

                        </div>
